This guide will help you set up your development environment, understand the architecture, and make your first contribution to Istiod, Istio's core control plane component.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [First Contribution Workflow](#first-contribution-workflow)\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### Required Go Version\n\nIstio requires **Go 1.25.0 or later**. Verify your installation:\n\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\n### Environment Setup\n\nIstio uses a modular build system that can operate in two modes:\n\n#### Option A: Native Build (Recommended for Development)\n\nIf you have Go toolchain installed locally, you can build directly:\n\n```bash\n# No additional setup needed - the Makefile will configure itself\nmake build\n```\n\n#### Option B: Container-Based Build\n\nTo use Docker for a reproducible build environment:\n\n```bash\nexport BUILD_WITH_CONTAINER=1\nmake build\n```\n\n**Note:** The build system will automatically detect your environment and set up necessary variables via `common/scripts/setup_env.sh`.\n\n### Cloning the Repository with Submodules\n\nClone Istio with all submodules:\n\n```bash\ngit clone --recurse-submodules https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nIf you've already cloned without submodules, initialize them:\n\n```bash\ngit submodule update --init --recursive\n```\n\n### Key Build Targets\n\nThe Istio build system provides several targets via `Makefile.core.mk`:\n\n#### Building Core Control Plane Binaries\n\n**Build all binaries (pilot-discovery, istioctl, pilot-agent):**\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis generates binaries in `$GOBIN` (typically `$GOPATH/bin`).\n\n**Build Linux-specific binaries (for container images):**\n\n```bash\nmake build-linux\n```\n\n**Build individual components:**\n\n```bash\n# pilot-discovery - the main XDS server and control plane\nmake pilot-discovery\n\n# istioctl - the command-line administration tool\nmake istioctl\n\n# pilot-agent - the data plane proxy agent\nmake pilot-agent\n```\n\n**Key binaries defined in Makefile.core.mk (lines 209-223):**\n\n- `./pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery` - Main control plane server\n- `./istioctl/cmd/istioctl` - CLI tool\n- `./pilot/cmd/pilot-agent` - Agent running on data plane\n- `./security/tools/generate_cert` - Certificate generation utility\n\n#### Understanding Build Dependencies\n\nThe build process depends on:\n\n1. **Envoy**: Downloaded by `make init` from pre-built artifacts\n2. **Go modules**: Managed through `go.mod` and `go.sum`\n3. **Protocol buffers**: Code generation handled by `tools/proto/proto.mk`\n\nTo initialize these dependencies:\n\n```bash\nmake init\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\n#### Unit Tests\n\nRun all unit tests with race condition detection:\n\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nThis internally runs `make racetest` and outputs JUnit-formatted results to `$ARTIFACTS/junit.xml`.\n\n**Run tests for a specific package:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\ngo test -race ./pkg/kube/inject/...\ngo test -race ./security/pkg/...\n```\n\n**Run tests with verbose output:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -v -race ./pilot/pkg/...\n```\n\n**Run fuzz tests:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -tags=integ ./tests/integration/pilot/...\n```\n\n#### Integration Tests\n\nIstio's integration tests require a Kubernetes cluster. They are tagged with the `integ` build tag:\n\n```bash\n# From the repository root, run integration tests\ngo test -tags=integ ./tests/integration/pilot/...\n```\n\nIntegration tests are located in `tests/integration/` and organized by component:\n\n- `tests/integration/pilot/` - Traffic management tests\n- `tests/integration/security/` - Security and mTLS tests\n- `tests/integration/ambient/` - Ambient mesh tests\n- `tests/integration/telemetry/` - Observability tests\n\n### Verifying Your Build\n\nAfter building, verify the binaries work:\n\n```bash\n# Check pilot-discovery help\n$GOPATH/bin/pilot-discovery --help\n\n# Check version\n$GOPATH/bin/pilot-discovery version\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components and Responsibilities\n\nIstiod is Istio's unified control plane, implementing what were historically three separate components:\n\n- **Pilot**: Manages traffic configuration (routing, load balancing, circuit breakers)\n- **Citadel**: Provides certificate management and mTLS security\n- **Galley**: Handles configuration distribution\n\nAll three are now merged into the single **istiod** binary (`pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`).\n\n#### Component Organization\n\n```\npilot/                          - Traffic management & service discovery\n├── pkg/xds/                    - XDS protocol implementation\n├── pkg/networking/             - Envoy config generation (routes, clusters, listeners)\n├── pkg/model/                  - Core data models (Proxy, PushContext, Service)\n├── pkg/config/                 - Kubernetes configuration ingestion\n├── pkg/serviceregistry/        - Service discovery from K8s/ServiceEntry\n└── cmd/pilot-discovery/        - Main entry point\n\nsecurity/                       - mTLS and certificate management\n├── pkg/ca/                     - Certificate authority implementation\n├── pkg/authn/                  - Authentication policy enforcement\n└── pkg/authz/                  - Authorization policy implementation\n\npkg/                            - Shared utilities\n├── kube/                       - Kubernetes client integration\n├── xds/                        - XDS server infrastructure\n├── model/                      - Shared data models\n└── ...\n```\n\n### The xDS Protocol: Service Configuration Delivery\n\nThe **xDS (Extensible Discovery Service)** protocol is the core mechanism through which Istiod pushes configuration to Envoy proxies (and other clients like gRPC, ztunnel).\n\n#### xDS Resource Types\n\nEnvoy clients request configuration through xDS:\n\n- **Listeners (LDS)**: Network listeners for incoming/outgoing traffic\n- **Routes (RDS)**: HTTP routing rules\n- **Clusters (CDS)**: Backend services and load balancing policies\n- **Endpoints (EDS)**: Individual service instances and their health status\n\nThese are interdependent: a route references a cluster, a listener references a route configuration.\n\n#### End-to-End Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's how a service discovery event flows through Istiod to update Envoy:\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes Event Occurs\n   └─> Pod starts/stops, Service scales, or ServiceEntry is created\n\n2. Service Discovery Layer (pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/)\n   └─> Detects changes via K8s informers\n   └─> Updates internal ServiceInstance and Service models\n\n3. Config Ingestion (architecture/networking/pilot.md)\n   └─> ConfigStore aggregates Kubernetes resources (Services, VirtualServices, DestinationRules)\n   └─> PushContext built - immutable snapshot of current configuration state\n\n4. Push Queue\n   └─> Change triggers debounce to avoid excessive updates\n   └─> Enqueued for all affected proxies\n   └─> Per-proxy merge logic ensures efficient batching\n\n5. Config Generation (pilot/pkg/networking/)\n   ├─> ClusterBuilder: Generates Envoy Clusters + Endpoints\n   ├─> ListenerBuilder: Generates Envoy Listeners\n   ├─> RouteBuilder: Generates VirtualHosts + Routes (RDS)\n   └─> Results are cached as protobuf.Any for reuse\n\n6. XDS Server (pilot/pkg/xds/)\n   └─> Sends generated config to Envoy over bidirectional gRPC stream\n   └─> Supports both SotW (State of the World) and Delta xDS protocols\n   └─> Tracks client subscriptions and only sends changed resources\n\n7. Envoy Applies Configuration\n   └─> Updates routing rules, load balancing, circuit breakers\n   └─> Traffic flows according to new configuration\n```\n\n### Key Packages and Their Roles\n\n#### pilot/pkg/xds/ - XDS Protocol Server\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/xds/`\n\nImplements the gRPC server that Envoy connects to:\n\n- `xds_server.go`: Main server accepting client connections\n- `xdsgen.go`: Config generation and versioning logic\n- `delta.go`: Delta xDS protocol implementation\n- `ads.go`: Aggregated Discovery Service (streaming requests)\n\n**Key concepts:**\n\n```go\n// DiscoveryServer - main server accepting xDS requests\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n    // Manages clients and subscriptions\n    // Triggers config pushes when changes occur\n}\n\n// Connection - represents a single Envoy proxy connection\ntype Connection struct {\n    proxy *model.Proxy\n    // Tracks subscribed resource types\n    // Handles bidirectional streaming\n}\n```\n\n**Example**: When a VirtualService is updated, the server:\n1. Detects the change\n2. Computes which proxies are affected\n3. Generates new Route configs via RouteGenerator\n4. Streams updates to affected clients\n\n#### pilot/pkg/networking/core/ - Envoy Config Builders\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`\n\nTranslates Istio configuration into Envoy protobuf format:\n\n- `cluster_builder.go`: Builds `Cluster` and `ClusterLoadAssignment` (endpoints)\n- `listener_builder.go`: Builds `Listener` with network/HTTP filters\n- `httproute.go`: Builds `RouteConfiguration` with virtual hosts and routes\n- `networkfilter.go`: Network-level filters (TCP, TLS)\n\n**Example usage in code**:\n\n```go\n// From pilot/pkg/xds/\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) generateClusters(proxy *model.Proxy, push *model.PushContext) {\n    cb := &clusterBuilder{proxy: proxy, req: req, push: push}\n    // Generates all Envoy Clusters for this proxy\n    clusters := cb.buildClusters()\n}\n```\n\n#### pilot/pkg/model/ - Core Data Structures\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/model/`\n\nCore types representing Istio's understanding of the service mesh:\n\n- `proxy.go`: `Proxy` - represents an Envoy sidecar/gateway\n- `context.go`: `PushContext` - immutable snapshot of configuration\n- `service.go`: `Service` - internal representation of a Kubernetes Service\n- `config.go`: `Config` - wrapper for all Istio resource types\n\n**PushContext structure** (key to efficiency):\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n    // Immutable snapshot of mesh state at a point in time\n    // Enables lock-free reads during config generation\n\n    // Indexes for fast lookups\n    services map[string]*Service\n    virtualServices map[string]*VirtualService\n    destinationRules map[string]*DestinationRule\n\n    // Per-proxy computed values\n    sidecarScopes map[string]*SidecarScope\n}\n```\n\n#### pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/ - Service Discovery\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`\n\nAggregates service information from multiple sources:\n\n- `kube/`: Kubernetes controller watching Services, Endpoints, Pods\n- `external.go`: ServiceEntry resources\n- `aggregate.go`: Merges all sources\n\n**Example**: When a Pod starts:\n\n```go\n// K8s informer detects Pod event\n// -> Updates Endpoints\n// -> ServiceDiscovery computes ServiceInstance\n// -> Triggers XDS push to affected proxies\n```\n\n#### security/pkg/ - Certificate and Policy Management\n\n**Location**: `security/pkg/`\n\nManages mTLS certificates and authorization:\n\n- `ca/`: Certificate authority implementation\n- `authn/`: Authentication (mutual TLS) policy\n- `authz/`: Authorization (RBAC) policy\n\n**Integration with Istiod**: Security policies are translated into Envoy filters during config generation:\n\n```go\n// In pilot/pkg/networking/\n// Security policies become Envoy filters in listener/route configuration\n```\n\n### Configuration Flow Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Config Ingestion                                         │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ • ConfigStore: K8s CRDs, ServiceEntry, Ingress         │\n│ • ServiceDiscovery: Services, Endpoints, Pods           │\n│ • Mesh Config: MeshConfig, Credentials                 │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ PushContext (Snapshot)                                   │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Immutable configuration state at a point in time        │\n│ Lock-free for concurrent reads during generation       │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Config Generators                                       │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ • RouteGenerator -> VirtualHost + Route                │\n│ • ClusterGenerator -> Cluster + Endpoints              │\n│ • ListenerGenerator -> Listener with Filters           │\n│ • SecurityGenerator -> mTLS and RBAC Filters          │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n        (Caching Layer - protobuf.Any)\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ XDS Server (pilot/pkg/xds/)                             │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Sends config to Envoy proxies over gRPC streams        │\n│ Supports State-of-World and Delta protocols            │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Envoy Proxies                                           │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Receive and apply routing, security, load balancing    │\n│ Enforce traffic policies at the data plane             │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding Good First Issues\n\nIstio uses GitHub Issues for tracking work. To find good starting points:\n\n1. **Visit the Istio GitHub repository**: https://github.com/istio/istio\n2. **Filter by labels**: Look for issues labeled:\n   - `kind/bug` - Bug fixes (often smaller scope)\n   - `area/...` - Your area of interest (e.g., `area/networking`, `area/security`)\n   - `good-first-issue` - Explicitly marked for newcomers\n   - `help-wanted` - Community contributions welcome\n\n3. **Read the issue description** to understand:\n   - What problem needs to be solved\n   - Where in the codebase the change belongs\n   - If it's blocked by other work\n\n4. **Comment on the issue** to express interest and get guidance from maintainers\n\n### Development Environment Setup\n\n#### 1. Fork and Clone\n\n```bash\n# Fork the repository via GitHub UI\n# Then clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/istio.git\ncd istio\n\n# Add upstream as a remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/istio/istio.git\n```\n\n#### 2. Create a Feature Branch\n\n```bash\n# Update from upstream first\ngit fetch upstream main\ngit checkout -b feature/my-feature upstream/main\n```\n\n#### 3. Install Development Tools\n\nThe build system will auto-detect and install needed tools. However, some useful tools to have:\n\n```bash\n# Protocol buffer compiler (for modifying APIs)\ngo install google.golang.org/protobuf/cmd/protoc-gen-go@latest\n\n# Code formatter\ngo install golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goimports@latest\n\n# Linter\ngo install github.com/golangci/golangci-lint/cmd/golangci-lint@latest\n\n# Test report generator (used by CI)\ngo install github.com/jstemmer/go-junit-report@latest\n```\n\n### Writing Code Changes\n\n#### Code Organization Principles\n\n1. **Keep changes minimal and focused** - One feature or bug fix per PR\n2. **Follow existing patterns** - Look at similar code in the package\n3. **Add or update tests** - Every change should have test coverage\n4. **Update documentation** - Comments for non-obvious logic\n\n#### Example: Adding a Feature to Pilot\n\nSuppose you're adding a new policy to route configuration:\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/networking/core/httproute.go\n// Find existing route generation code\n// Add your policy translation alongside similar logic\n\nfunc (rg *routeConfigGenerator) buildHTTPRoutes(...) {\n    // Existing code...\n\n    // Your new policy handling\n    if policy := push.GetMyNewPolicy(routeName); policy != nil {\n        // Apply policy to route configuration\n        route.MyPolicyConfig = translatePolicy(policy)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Example: Adding Security Policy\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/networking/core/listener.go\n// Security policies become Envoy filters\n\nfunc (lb *ListenerBuilder) buildHTTPFilters(...) {\n    filters := []*hcm.HttpFilter{}\n\n    // Existing filters...\n\n    // Your security policy filter\n    if authzPolicy := lb.push.AuthorizationPolicy(lb.node); authzPolicy != nil {\n        filters = append(filters, buildAuthzFilter(authzPolicy))\n    }\n\n    return filters\n}\n```\n\n### Running Linters and Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore committing, run the pre-commit checks:\n\n```bash\n# Format all code and run basic linters\nmake format\n\n# Full linting suite (may take a minute)\nmake lint\n```\n\n**What these do:**\n\n- `format`: Auto-formats Go code, fixes import order\n- `lint`: Checks code style, copyright headers, Python/shell scripts, YAML, Helm charts\n\n**Key targets from Makefile.core.mk (line 287-290):**\n\n```makefile\nlint: lint-python lint-copyright-banner lint-scripts lint-go \\\n      lint-dockerfiles lint-markdown lint-yaml lint-licenses lint-helm-global\n```\n\n#### Checking Your Specific Changes\n\n```bash\n# Only lint your package\ncd pilot/pkg/xds\ngo vet ./...\ngolangci-lint run ./...\n\n# Format just your files\ngoimports -w *.go\n```\n\n### Writing and Running Unit Tests\n\n#### Test Structure\n\nIstio uses standard Go testing. Tests live alongside code with `_test.go` suffix:\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/xds/xds_test.go\npackage xds\n\nimport \"testing\"\n\nfunc TestGenerateClusterName(t *testing.T) {\n    // Arrange\n    proxy := &model.Proxy{ID: \"sleep-1\"}\n\n    // Act\n    name := generateClusterName(proxy, \"productpage\")\n\n    // Assert\n    if name != \"outbound|9080||productpage.default.svc.cluster.local\" {\n        t.Errorf(\"got %s, want expected name\", name)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Running Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run tests for your package\ngo test -v ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run a specific test\ngo test -v -run TestGenerateClusterName ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run with race detector (catches concurrency bugs)\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run all tests and generate coverage report\ngo test -race -coverprofile=coverage.out ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\ngo tool cover -html=coverage.out  # View in browser\n```\n\n#### Testing Controller Logic\n\nFor controllers and service discovery changes, Istio provides testing utilities:\n\n```go\n// From architecture/networking/controllers.md\n// See pkg/kube/controllers/example_test.go for reference\n\nfunc TestMyController(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use the Example Controller pattern for proper testing\n    // This handles the subtleties of controller testing\n}\n```\n\n**Key testing packages:**\n\n- `pkg/test/util/assert` - Assertion utilities\n- `pkg/kube/kclient/clienttest` - Fake Kubernetes clients for unit tests\n- `pkg/test/framework` - Integration test framework\n\n### Submitting a Pull Request\n\n#### 1. Commit Your Changes\n\n```bash\n# Review your changes\ngit diff\n\n# Stage changes\ngit add pilot/pkg/xds/my_change.go\ngit add pilot/pkg/xds/my_change_test.go\n\n# Commit with clear message\ngit commit -m \"Fix XDS push for VirtualService updates\n\nWhen a VirtualService is updated, affected proxies now receive\nimmediate configuration updates instead of waiting for the next\npush cycle. Verify your installation:\n\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\n### Environment Setup\n\nIstio uses a modular build system that can operate in two modes:\n\n#### Option A: Native Build (Recommended for Development)\n\nIf you have Go toolchain installed locally, you can build directly:\n\n```bash\n# No additional setup needed - the Makefile will configure itself\nmake build\n```\n\n#### Option B: Container-Based Build\n\nTo use Docker for a reproducible build environment:\n\n```bash\nexport BUILD_WITH_CONTAINER=1\nmake build\n```\n\n**Note:** The build system will automatically detect your environment and set up necessary variables via `common/scripts/setup_env.sh`.\n\n### Cloning the Repository with Submodules\n\nClone Istio with all submodules:\n\n```bash\ngit clone --recurse-submodules https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nIf you've already cloned without submodules, initialize them:\n\n```bash\ngit submodule update --init --recursive\n```\n\n### Key Build Targets\n\nThe Istio build system provides several targets via `Makefile.core.mk`:\n\n#### Building Core Control Plane Binaries\n\n**Build all binaries (pilot-discovery, istioctl, pilot-agent):**\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis generates binaries in `$GOBIN` (typically `$GOPATH/bin`).\n\n**Build Linux-specific binaries (for container images):**\n\n```bash\nmake build-linux\n```\n\n**Build individual components:**\n\n```bash\n# pilot-discovery - the main XDS server and control plane\nmake pilot-discovery\n\n# istioctl - the command-line administration tool\nmake istioctl\n\n# pilot-agent - the data plane proxy agent\nmake pilot-agent\n```\n\n**Key binaries defined in Makefile.core.mk (lines 209-223):**\n\n- `./pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery` - Main control plane server\n- `./istioctl/cmd/istioctl` - CLI tool\n- `./pilot/cmd/pilot-agent` - Agent running on data plane\n- `./security/tools/generate_cert` - Certificate generation utility\n\n#### Understanding Build Dependencies\n\nThe build process depends on:\n\n1. **Envoy**: Downloaded by `make init` from pre-built artifacts\n2. **Go modules**: Managed through `go.mod` and `go.sum`\n3. **Protocol buffers**: Code generation handled by `tools/proto/proto.mk`\n\nTo initialize these dependencies:\n\n```bash\nmake init\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\n#### Unit Tests\n\nRun all unit tests with race condition detection:\n\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nThis internally runs `make racetest` and outputs JUnit-formatted results to `$ARTIFACTS/junit.xml`.\n\n**Run tests for a specific package:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\ngo test -race ./pkg/kube/inject/...\ngo test -race ./security/pkg/...\n```\n\n**Run tests with verbose output:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -v -race ./pilot/pkg/...\n```\n\n**Run fuzz tests:**\n\n```bash\ngo test -tags=integ ./tests/integration/pilot/...\n```\n\n#### Integration Tests\n\nIstio's integration tests require a Kubernetes cluster. They are tagged with the `integ` build tag:\n\n```bash\n# From the repository root, run integration tests\ngo test -tags=integ ./tests/integration/pilot/...\n```\n\nIntegration tests are located in `tests/integration/` and organized by component:\n\n- `tests/integration/pilot/` - Traffic management tests\n- `tests/integration/security/` - Security and mTLS tests\n- `tests/integration/ambient/` - Ambient mesh tests\n- `tests/integration/telemetry/` - Observability tests\n\n### Verifying Your Build\n\nAfter building, verify the binaries work:\n\n```bash\n# Check pilot-discovery help\n$GOPATH/bin/pilot-discovery --help\n\n# Check version\n$GOPATH/bin/pilot-discovery version\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components and Responsibilities\n\nIstiod is Istio's unified control plane, implementing what were historically three separate components:\n\n- **Pilot**: Manages traffic configuration (routing, load balancing, circuit breakers)\n- **Citadel**: Provides certificate management and mTLS security\n- **Galley**: Handles configuration distribution\n\nAll three are now merged into the single **istiod** binary (`pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`).\n\n#### Component Organization\n\n```\npilot/                          - Traffic management & service discovery\n├── pkg/xds/                    - XDS protocol implementation\n├── pkg/networking/             - Envoy config generation (routes, clusters, listeners)\n├── pkg/model/                  - Core data models (Proxy, PushContext, Service)\n├── pkg/config/                 - Kubernetes configuration ingestion\n├── pkg/serviceregistry/        - Service discovery from K8s/ServiceEntry\n└── cmd/pilot-discovery/        - Main entry point\n\nsecurity/                       - mTLS and certificate management\n├── pkg/ca/                     - Certificate authority implementation\n├── pkg/authn/                  - Authentication policy enforcement\n└── pkg/authz/                  - Authorization policy implementation\n\npkg/                            - Shared utilities\n├── kube/                       - Kubernetes client integration\n├── xds/                        - XDS server infrastructure\n├── model/                      - Shared data models\n└── ...\n```\n\n### The xDS Protocol: Service Configuration Delivery\n\nThe **xDS (Extensible Discovery Service)** protocol is the core mechanism through which Istiod pushes configuration to Envoy proxies (and other clients like gRPC, ztunnel).\n\n#### xDS Resource Types\n\nEnvoy clients request configuration through xDS:\n\n- **Listeners (LDS)**: Network listeners for incoming/outgoing traffic\n- **Routes (RDS)**: HTTP routing rules\n- **Clusters (CDS)**: Backend services and load balancing policies\n- **Endpoints (EDS)**: Individual service instances and their health status\n\nThese are interdependent: a route references a cluster, a listener references a route configuration.\n\n#### End-to-End Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's how a service discovery event flows through Istiod to update Envoy:\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes Event Occurs\n   └─> Pod starts/stops, Service scales, or ServiceEntry is created\n\n2. Service Discovery Layer (pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/)\n   └─> Detects changes via K8s informers\n   └─> Updates internal ServiceInstance and Service models\n\n3. Config Ingestion (architecture/networking/pilot.md)\n   └─> ConfigStore aggregates Kubernetes resources (Services, VirtualServices, DestinationRules)\n   └─> PushContext built - immutable snapshot of current configuration state\n\n4. Push Queue\n   └─> Change triggers debounce to avoid excessive updates\n   └─> Enqueued for all affected proxies\n   └─> Per-proxy merge logic ensures efficient batching\n\n5. Config Generation (pilot/pkg/networking/)\n   ├─> ClusterBuilder: Generates Envoy Clusters + Endpoints\n   ├─> ListenerBuilder: Generates Envoy Listeners\n   ├─> RouteBuilder: Generates VirtualHosts + Routes (RDS)\n   └─> Results are cached as protobuf.Any for reuse\n\n6. XDS Server (pilot/pkg/xds/)\n   └─> Sends generated config to Envoy over bidirectional gRPC stream\n   └─> Supports both SotW (State of the World) and Delta xDS protocols\n   └─> Tracks client subscriptions and only sends changed resources\n\n7. Envoy Applies Configuration\n   └─> Updates routing rules, load balancing, circuit breakers\n   └─> Traffic flows according to new configuration\n```\n\n### Key Packages and Their Roles\n\n#### pilot/pkg/xds/ - XDS Protocol Server\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/xds/`\n\nImplements the gRPC server that Envoy connects to:\n\n- `xds_server.go`: Main server accepting client connections\n- `xdsgen.go`: Config generation and versioning logic\n- `delta.go`: Delta xDS protocol implementation\n- `ads.go`: Aggregated Discovery Service (streaming requests)\n\n**Key concepts:**\n\n```go\n// DiscoveryServer - main server accepting xDS requests\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n    // Manages clients and subscriptions\n    // Triggers config pushes when changes occur\n}\n\n// Connection - represents a single Envoy proxy connection\ntype Connection struct {\n    proxy *model.Proxy\n    // Tracks subscribed resource types\n    // Handles bidirectional streaming\n}\n```\n\n**Example**: When a VirtualService is updated, the server:\n1. Detects the change\n2. Computes which proxies are affected\n3. Generates new Route configs via RouteGenerator\n4. Streams updates to affected clients\n\n#### pilot/pkg/networking/core/ - Envoy Config Builders\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`\n\nTranslates Istio configuration into Envoy protobuf format:\n\n- `cluster_builder.go`: Builds `Cluster` and `ClusterLoadAssignment` (endpoints)\n- `listener_builder.go`: Builds `Listener` with network/HTTP filters\n- `httproute.go`: Builds `RouteConfiguration` with virtual hosts and routes\n- `networkfilter.go`: Network-level filters (TCP, TLS)\n\n**Example usage in code**:\n\n```go\n// From pilot/pkg/xds/\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) generateClusters(proxy *model.Proxy, push *model.PushContext) {\n    cb := &clusterBuilder{proxy: proxy, req: req, push: push}\n    // Generates all Envoy Clusters for this proxy\n    clusters := cb.buildClusters()\n}\n```\n\n#### pilot/pkg/model/ - Core Data Structures\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/model/`\n\nCore types representing Istio's understanding of the service mesh:\n\n- `proxy.go`: `Proxy` - represents an Envoy sidecar/gateway\n- `context.go`: `PushContext` - immutable snapshot of configuration\n- `service.go`: `Service` - internal representation of a Kubernetes Service\n- `config.go`: `Config` - wrapper for all Istio resource types\n\n**PushContext structure** (key to efficiency):\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n    // Immutable snapshot of mesh state at a point in time\n    // Enables lock-free reads during config generation\n\n    // Indexes for fast lookups\n    services map[string]*Service\n    virtualServices map[string]*VirtualService\n    destinationRules map[string]*DestinationRule\n\n    // Per-proxy computed values\n    sidecarScopes map[string]*SidecarScope\n}\n```\n\n#### pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/ - Service Discovery\n\n**Location**: `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`\n\nAggregates service information from multiple sources:\n\n- `kube/`: Kubernetes controller watching Services, Endpoints, Pods\n- `external.go`: ServiceEntry resources\n- `aggregate.go`: Merges all sources\n\n**Example**: When a Pod starts:\n\n```go\n// K8s informer detects Pod event\n// -> Updates Endpoints\n// -> ServiceDiscovery computes ServiceInstance\n// -> Triggers XDS push to affected proxies\n```\n\n#### security/pkg/ - Certificate and Policy Management\n\n**Location**: `security/pkg/`\n\nManages mTLS certificates and authorization:\n\n- `ca/`: Certificate authority implementation\n- `authn/`: Authentication (mutual TLS) policy\n- `authz/`: Authorization (RBAC) policy\n\n**Integration with Istiod**: Security policies are translated into Envoy filters during config generation:\n\n```go\n// In pilot/pkg/networking/\n// Security policies become Envoy filters in listener/route configuration\n```\n\n### Configuration Flow Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Config Ingestion                                         │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ • ConfigStore: K8s CRDs, ServiceEntry, Ingress         │\n│ • ServiceDiscovery: Services, Endpoints, Pods           │\n│ • Mesh Config: MeshConfig, Credentials                 │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ PushContext (Snapshot)                                   │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Immutable configuration state at a point in time        │\n│ Lock-free for concurrent reads during generation       │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Config Generators                                       │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ • RouteGenerator -> VirtualHost + Route                │\n│ • ClusterGenerator -> Cluster + Endpoints              │\n│ • ListenerGenerator -> Listener with Filters           │\n│ • SecurityGenerator -> mTLS and RBAC Filters          │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n        (Caching Layer - protobuf.Any)\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ XDS Server (pilot/pkg/xds/)                             │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Sends config to Envoy proxies over gRPC streams        │\n│ Supports State-of-World and Delta protocols            │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Envoy Proxies                                           │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ Receive and apply routing, security, load balancing    │\n│ Enforce traffic policies at the data plane             │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding Good First Issues\n\nIstio uses GitHub Issues for tracking work. To find good starting points:\n\n1. **Visit the Istio GitHub repository**: https://github.com/istio/istio\n2. **Filter by labels**: Look for issues labeled:\n   - `kind/bug` - Bug fixes (often smaller scope)\n   - `area/...` - Your area of interest (e.g., `area/networking`, `area/security`)\n   - `good-first-issue` - Explicitly marked for newcomers\n   - `help-wanted` - Community contributions welcome\n\n3. **Read the issue description** to understand:\n   - What problem needs to be solved\n   - Where in the codebase the change belongs\n   - If it's blocked by other work\n\n4. **Comment on the issue** to express interest and get guidance from maintainers\n\n### Development Environment Setup\n\n#### 1. Fork and Clone\n\n```bash\n# Fork the repository via GitHub UI\n# Then clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/istio.git\ncd istio\n\n# Add upstream as a remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/istio/istio.git\n```\n\n#### 2. Create a Feature Branch\n\n```bash\n# Update from upstream first\ngit fetch upstream main\ngit checkout -b feature/my-feature upstream/main\n```\n\n#### 3. Install Development Tools\n\nThe build system will auto-detect and install needed tools. However, some useful tools to have:\n\n```bash\n# Protocol buffer compiler (for modifying APIs)\ngo install google.golang.org/protobuf/cmd/protoc-gen-go@latest\n\n# Code formatter\ngo install golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goimports@latest\n\n# Linter\ngo install github.com/golangci/golangci-lint/cmd/golangci-lint@latest\n\n# Test report generator (used by CI)\ngo install github.com/jstemmer/go-junit-report@latest\n```\n\n### Writing Code Changes\n\n#### Code Organization Principles\n\n1. **Keep changes minimal and focused** - One feature or bug fix per PR\n2. **Follow existing patterns** - Look at similar code in the package\n3. **Add or update tests** - Every change should have test coverage\n4. **Update documentation** - Comments for non-obvious logic\n\n#### Example: Adding a Feature to Pilot\n\nSuppose you're adding a new policy to route configuration:\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/networking/core/httproute.go\n// Find existing route generation code\n// Add your policy translation alongside similar logic\n\nfunc (rg *routeConfigGenerator) buildHTTPRoutes(...) {\n    // Existing code...\n\n    // Your new policy handling\n    if policy := push.GetMyNewPolicy(routeName); policy != nil {\n        // Apply policy to route configuration\n        route.MyPolicyConfig = translatePolicy(policy)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Example: Adding Security Policy\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/networking/core/listener.go\n// Security policies become Envoy filters\n\nfunc (lb *ListenerBuilder) buildHTTPFilters(...) {\n    filters := []*hcm.HttpFilter{}\n\n    // Existing filters...\n\n    // Your security policy filter\n    if authzPolicy := lb.push.AuthorizationPolicy(lb.node); authzPolicy != nil {\n        filters = append(filters, buildAuthzFilter(authzPolicy))\n    }\n\n    return filters\n}\n```\n\n### Running Linters and Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore committing, run the pre-commit checks:\n\n```bash\n# Format all code and run basic linters\nmake format\n\n# Full linting suite (may take a minute)\nmake lint\n```\n\n**What these do:**\n\n- `format`: Auto-formats Go code, fixes import order\n- `lint`: Checks code style, copyright headers, Python/shell scripts, YAML, Helm charts\n\n**Key targets from Makefile.core.mk (line 287-290):**\n\n```makefile\nlint: lint-python lint-copyright-banner lint-scripts lint-go \\\n      lint-dockerfiles lint-markdown lint-yaml lint-licenses lint-helm-global\n```\n\n#### Checking Your Specific Changes\n\n```bash\n# Only lint your package\ncd pilot/pkg/xds\ngo vet ./...\ngolangci-lint run ./...\n\n# Format just your files\ngoimports -w *.go\n```\n\n### Writing and Running Unit Tests\n\n#### Test Structure\n\nIstio uses standard Go testing. Tests live alongside code with `_test.go` suffix:\n\n```go\n// File: pilot/pkg/xds/xds_test.go\npackage xds\n\nimport \"testing\"\n\nfunc TestGenerateClusterName(t *testing.T) {\n    // Arrange\n    proxy := &model.Proxy{ID: \"sleep-1\"}\n\n    // Act\n    name := generateClusterName(proxy, \"productpage\")\n\n    // Assert\n    if name != \"outbound|9080||productpage.default.svc.cluster.local\" {\n        t.Errorf(\"got %s, want expected name\", name)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Running Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run tests for your package\ngo test -v ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run a specific test\ngo test -v -run TestGenerateClusterName ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run with race detector (catches concurrency bugs)\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# Run all tests and generate coverage report\ngo test -race -coverprofile=coverage.out ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\ngo tool cover -html=coverage.out  # View in browser\n```\n\n#### Testing Controller Logic\n\nFor controllers and service discovery changes, Istio provides testing utilities:\n\n```go\n// From architecture/networking/controllers.md\n// See pkg/kube/controllers/example_test.go for reference\n\nfunc TestMyController(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use the Example Controller pattern for proper testing\n    // This handles the subtleties of controller testing\n}\n```\n\n**Key testing packages:**\n\n- `pkg/test/util/assert` - Assertion utilities\n- `pkg/kube/kclient/clienttest` - Fake Kubernetes clients for unit tests\n- `pkg/test/framework` - Integration test framework\n\n### Submitting a Pull Request\n\n#### 1. Commit Your Changes\n\n```bash\n# Review your changes\ngit diff\n\n# Stage changes\ngit add pilot/pkg/xds/my_change.go\ngit add pilot/pkg/xds/my_change_test.go\n\n# Commit with clear message\ngit commit -m \"Fix XDS push for VirtualService updates\n\nWhen a VirtualService is updated, affected proxies now receive\nimmediate configuration updates instead of waiting for the next\npush cycle. This reduces latency from configuration changes.\n\nFixes #<issue-number>\"\n```\n\n**Commit message guidelines:**\n- First line: short summary (50 chars max)\n- Blank line\n- Detailed explanation of what and why\n- Reference GitHub issues with \"Fixes #<number>\"\n\n#### 2. Push to Your Fork\n\n```bash\ngit push origin feature/my-feature\n```\n\n#### 3. Create Pull Request\n\nVisit GitHub and create a PR from your fork's branch to upstream `main`.\n\n**PR Template** (auto-populated from `.github/pull_request_template.md`):\n\n- Describe what problem this solves\n- Check the affected areas (Networking, Security, Testing, etc.)\n- Note if this has user-facing changes (requires release notes)\n- Link related issues\n\n**Example PR description:**\n\n```markdown\n**Description:**\nImproves efficiency of xDS pushes by skipping unnecessary updates to\ngateways that don't have listeners on modified routes.\n\n**Areas Affected:**\n- [x] Networking\n- [x] Performance and Scalability\n\n**User-facing:**\n- [ ] Does not have any user-facing changes\n```\n\n#### 4. Required Checks Pass\n\nGitHub will automatically run:\n\n- **Unit tests**: `make test` equivalent\n- **Linters**: `make lint` equivalent\n- **Build verification**: `make build` equivalent\n\nAll must pass before merge. If CI fails:\n\n1. Review the failure details\n2. Fix the issue locally\n3. Push the fix to your branch\n4. CI automatically re-runs\n\n#### 5. Code Review\n\nIstio reviewers will:\n\n1. **Review code quality** - Does it follow patterns, handle edge cases?\n2. **Check for performance impact** - Does it add unnecessary allocations/copies?\n3. **Verify test coverage** - Are changes adequately tested?\n4. **Ensure documentation** - Are comments clear for future maintainers?\n\n**Responding to feedback:**\n\n```bash\n# Make requested changes\n# ... edit files ...\n\n# Commit (no need to squash - maintainers do that)\ngit commit -m \"Address code review feedback\"\ngit push origin feature/my-feature\n```\n\n#### 6. Merge and Cleanup\n\nOnce approved:\n\n1. Maintainer merges your PR\n2. Delete your feature branch: `git branch -d feature/my-feature`\n3. Update your fork: `git fetch upstream && git rebase upstream/main`\n\n### Release Notes\n\n**When to add release notes:**\n\nRelease notes are required for:\n- New features\n- Bug fixes with user impact\n- Performance improvements\n- Breaking changes\n\n**Not required for:**\n- Tests\n- Build infrastructure\n- Internal refactoring\n\n**Adding a release note:**\n\n1. Create `releasenotes/notes/<ISSUE>.<NOTE-TYPE>.yaml`:\n\n```yaml\n# Example: releasenotes/notes/12345.bug-fix.yaml\napiVersion: release.istio.io/v1alpha1\nkind: BugFix\nmetadata:\n  title: Fix VirtualService update latency\n\ndescription: |\n  Fixed a performance issue where VirtualService updates could take\n  up to 5 seconds to propagate to affected proxies. Updates now\n  propagate in <100ms in most cases.\n---\n```\n\n2. Valid note types:\n   - `feature` - New feature\n   - `bug-fix` - Bug fix\n   - `upgrade` - Breaking changes or migration needed\n   - `deprecation` - API deprecation\n\n### Testing Your Complete Change\n\nBefore pushing for review, verify everything locally:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Build\nmake build\n\n# 2. Run all tests for your package\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/xds/...\n\n# 3. Run linters\nmake format\nmake lint\n\n# 4. For integration changes, test with a cluster if possible\n# (requires Kubernetes cluster)\ngo test -tags=integ -v ./tests/integration/pilot/...\n```\n\n### Debugging and Troubleshooting\n\n#### Common Issues\n\n**Issue**: Tests fail with import errors\n```bash\n# Fix: Download Go modules\ngo mod download\ngo mod tidy\n```\n\n**Issue**: Linter complains about formatting\n```bash\n# Fix: Auto-format\nmake format\n```\n\n**Issue**: Build fails with \"command not found\"\n```bash\n# Fix: Initialize build environment\nmake init\nmake depend\n```\n\n#### Useful Development Commands\n\n```bash\n# Show environment variables used by build\nmake show.env\n\n# Show Go environment\nmake show.goenv\n\n# Clean all build artifacts\nmake clean\n\n# View a specific variable\nmake show.VERSION\n```\n\n#### Debugging Pilot Code\n\nFor debugging Istiod behavior:\n\n1. **Add debug logs**:\n\n```go\nimport \"istio.io/istio/pkg/log\"\n\nfunc MyFunction(proxy *model.Proxy) {\n    log.Debugf(\"Processing proxy %s with config version %d\", proxy.ID, version)\n}\n```\n\n2. **Run with debug output**:\n\n```bash\n# Set log level\nLOG_LEVEL=debug make build\n```\n\n3. **Use istioctl for inspection**:\n\n```bash\n# View proxy configuration\nistioctl proxy-config cluster <pod-name> -n <namespace>\n\n# View routes\nistioctl proxy-config routes <pod-name> -n <namespace>\n\n# Compare configurations\nistioctl analyze  # Check for configuration issues\n```\n\n---\n\n## Resources and References\n\n### Key Documentation Files\n\n- `architecture/networking/pilot.md` -
